## PHASE: P2 credibility-skill (#1151) — DIFF gate iter 1. The BRIEF was Codex-APPROVED iter 2 (.codex/I-cred-002/codex_brief_verdict_iter2.txt — 0 P0/P1, accept_remaining). +"""I-cred-002 (Phase 2, L1 / §9.1) — adaptive LLM credibility skill (reliability × relevance).
```diff
+
+ONE generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill. Per research question it scores EACH candidate
+source on RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE with a written, inspectable rationale, consuming POLARIS's
+already-computed deterministic authority signals (``authority_score`` / ``source_class`` /
+``corroboration_count`` / ``authority_confidence`` / ``signal_scores`` / ``junk_class`` /
+``predatory_oa``) as its PRIORS. There are NO fixed domain rubrics: the detected ``domain`` is a
+single HINT field the judge reasons over, never a branch that swaps rubrics — so this scales to any
+field (operator directive 2026-06-08, plan §9.1).
+
+FAITHFULNESS POSTURE (binding):
+  * ADVISORY ONLY. This never becomes a faithfulness gate — ``strict_verify``'s six per-sentence
+    checks (``generator/provenance_generator.py``) remain the ONLY binding gate. A credibility
+    weight/rationale is a side-output to disclose, never a reason to keep or drop a sentence.
+  * DEFAULT-OFF byte-identical: ``PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL`` (no production caller is added here).
+  * The LLM call is DEPENDENCY-INJECTED (``judge``); with no judge → no network, no client, no spend
+    (mirrors ``retrieval/semantic_conflict_detector``). The production judge is wired by the caller,
+    never constructed in this pure library.
+  * NO row mutation, NO faithfulness-file import. Pure functions, snake_case, explicit imports.
+  * LAW VI: every threshold is an env-overridable named constant (no magic numbers, no hardcoded
+    model/endpoint).
+
+ANTI-FABRICATION (the LOW/thin guardrail): for a LOW-confidence or thin-signal source the judge's
+reliability is capped at ``clamp01(authority_score) + PG_CREDIBILITY_MAX_UPLIFT`` — the model cannot
+invent authority that the deterministic signals do not support. The judge MAY freely DOWN-rate any
+source below its prior (a high-authority but irrelevant/weak source can score low); the prior is NOT
+a lower bound. The deterministic priors-only judgment is the fallback ONLY on a judge error / no
+judge, never a universal floor.
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import math
+import os
+from dataclasses import dataclass, field
+from typing import Any, Callable, Optional
+
+# ── flag (default OFF — matches supersession.py / claim_graph.py) ─────────────
+_FLAG = "PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL"
+_OFF_VALUES = frozenset({"", "0", "false", "off", "no"})
+
+# ── env knobs (LAW VI: named, env-overridable, no magic numbers) ──────────────
+_ENV_MAX_UPLIFT = "PG_CREDIBILITY_MAX_UPLIFT"
+_ENV_SNIPPET_CHARS = "PG_CREDIBILITY_SNIPPET_CHARS"
+_DEFAULT_MAX_UPLIFT = 0.15
+_DEFAULT_SNIPPET_CHARS = 1200
+
+# The deterministic prior-signal names the judge may cite (anti-hallucination: a
+# ``signals_cited`` entry that is not one of these AND present on the row is dropped).
+_PRIOR_SIGNAL_KEYS = (
+    "authority_score",
+    "source_class",
+    "corroboration_count",
+    "authority_confidence",
+    "signal_scores",
+    "junk_class",
+    "predatory_oa",
+)
+
+
+def credibility_skill_enabled() -> bool:
+    """True unless ``PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL`` is unset/falsey (default OFF => byte-identical).
+
+    Caller kill-switch: no production caller invokes this library while OFF, so the rendered report
+    + manifest are unchanged. The pure functions below do NOT read the flag — they are total +
+    offline-testable; the caller gates invocation.
+    """
+    return os.environ.get(_FLAG, "").strip().lower() not in _OFF_VALUES
+
+
+def _float_env(name: str, default: float) -> float:
+    try:
+        return float(os.environ.get(name, "") or default)
+    except (TypeError, ValueError):
+        return default
+
+
+def _int_env(name: str, default: int) -> int:
+    try:
+        return int(os.environ.get(name, "") or default)
+    except (TypeError, ValueError):
+        return default
+
+
+def _clamp01(value: Any) -> float | None:
+    """Clamp a numeric to [0, 1]. Returns ``None`` for non-numeric / NaN / inf (the caller treats
+    that as a judge error — never a NaN weight, never a crash)."""
+    try:
+        x = float(value)
+    except (TypeError, ValueError):
+        return None
+    if math.isnan(x) or math.isinf(x):
+        return None
+    return 0.0 if x < 0.0 else 1.0 if x > 1.0 else x
+
+
+@dataclass
+class CredibilityJudgment:
+    """One source's advisory credibility judgment (a side-output, never a verdict input).
+
+    ``reliability_score`` is AFTER the anti-fabrication cap; ``relevance_score`` is the judged
+    directness to the question (unknown => 1.0, multiplicative-neutral); ``credibility_weight`` is
+    the FIXED product ``clamp01(reliability * relevance)``. ``signals_cited`` is the subset of the
+    deterministic prior signals the judge reasoned from. ``judge_error`` is True iff the injected
+    judge raised / returned malformed output for THIS source (isolated; priors-only fallback used).
+    """
+
+    evidence_id: str
+    reliability_score: float
+    relevance_score: float
+    credibility_weight: float
+    rationale: str
+    signals_cited: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)
+    query_need: str = ""
+    judge_error: bool = False
+
+
+def _present_signals(row: dict[str, Any]) -> list[str]:
+    """The deterministic prior signals actually present (non-empty) on this row."""
+    return [k for k in _PRIOR_SIGNAL_KEYS if row.get(k) not in (None, "", {}, [])]
+
+
+def _row_snippet(row: dict[str, Any], max_chars: int) -> str:
+    text = str(row.get("direct_quote") or row.get("statement") or row.get("text") or "")
+    return text[:max_chars]
+
+
+def _build_judge_payload(
+    research_question: str, row: dict[str, Any], domain: str | None
+) -> dict[str, Any]:
+    """Pure: assemble the judge payload for ONE source. Does NOT mutate ``row``.
+
+    Carries source identity + bounded descriptors (title / url / snippet — so RELEVANCE is actually
+    judgeable) + the deterministic authority priors + the ``domain_hint`` (a single string field,
+    NOT a branch / rubric table). The judge sees ONLY this payload.
+    """
+    snippet_chars = _int_env(_ENV_SNIPPET_CHARS, _DEFAULT_SNIPPET_CHARS)
+    return {
+        "research_question": research_question,
+        "evidence_id": str(row.get("evidence_id", "")),
+        "title": str(row.get("title", "") or ""),
+        "url": str(row.get("source_url", "") or row.get("url", "") or ""),
+        "snippet": _row_snippet(row, snippet_chars),
+        "authority_score": row.get("authority_score"),
+        "source_class": row.get("source_class"),
+        "corroboration_count": row.get("corroboration_count"),
+        "authority_confidence": row.get("authority_confidence"),
+        "signal_scores": dict(row.get("signal_scores") or {}),
+        "junk_class": row.get("junk_class", ""),
+        "predatory_oa": row.get("predatory_oa", False),
+        "domain_hint": domain or "",
+    }
+
+
+def _is_low_or_thin(row: dict[str, Any]) -> bool:
+    """A source is LOW/thin (subject to the anti-fabrication cap) when its authority_confidence is
+    LOW, or it has no authority_score, or it has no signal_scores."""
+    if str(row.get("authority_confidence") or "").strip().upper() == "LOW":
+        return True
+    if row.get("authority_score") is None:
+        return True
+    if not (row.get("signal_scores") or {}):
+        return True
+    return False
+
+
+def _priors_only_judgment(row: dict[str, Any]) -> CredibilityJudgment:
+    """The deterministic fallback (no judge / judge error): reliability from the prior, relevance
+    neutral (1.0). Never fabricates relevance it cannot judge."""
+    auth = _clamp01(row.get("authority_score"))
+    reliability = auth if auth is not None else 0.0
+    return CredibilityJudgment(
+        evidence_id=str(row.get("evidence_id", "")),
+        reliability_score=reliability,
+        relevance_score=1.0,
+        credibility_weight=reliability,  # == clamp01(reliability * 1.0)
+        rationale="no judge wired — deterministic priors only",
+        signals_cited=_present_signals(row),
+        query_need="",
+        judge_error=False,
+    )
+
+
+def _apply_judge(
+    research_question: str,
+    row: dict[str, Any],
+    domain: str | None,
+    judge: Callable[[str, dict], dict],
+) -> CredibilityJudgment:
+    """Run the injected judge for ONE source; fall back to priors on ANY error / malformed output
+    (isolated to this row — recall-first, fail-loud-but-bounded)."""
+    payload = _build_judge_payload(research_question, row, domain)
+    try:
+        raw = judge(research_question, payload)
+    except Exception:
+        fallback = _priors_only_judgment(row)
+        fallback.judge_error = True
+        return fallback
+    if not isinstance(raw, dict):
+        fallback = _priors_only_judgment(row)
+        fallback.judge_error = True
+        return fallback
+
+    reliability = _clamp01(raw.get("reliability_score"))
+    if reliability is None:  # missing / NaN / inf reliability => judge error for this row
+        fallback = _priors_only_judgment(row)
+        fallback.judge_error = True
+        return fallback
+    relevance = _clamp01(raw.get("relevance_score"))
+    if relevance is None:  # unknown / malformed relevance => multiplicative-neutral
+        relevance = 1.0
+
+    # Anti-fabrication cap: a LOW/thin source's reliability cannot exceed prior + max_uplift.
+    if _is_low_or_thin(row):
+        auth = _clamp01(row.get("authority_score")) or 0.0
+        cap = _clamp01(auth + _float_env(_ENV_MAX_UPLIFT, _DEFAULT_MAX_UPLIFT))
+        if cap is not None:
+            reliability = min(reliability, cap)
+
+    present = set(_present_signals(row))
+    cited = [s for s in (raw.get("signals_cited") or []) if s in present]
+    weight = _clamp01(reliability * relevance)
+    return CredibilityJudgment(
+        evidence_id=str(row.get("evidence_id", "")),
+        reliability_score=reliability,
+        relevance_score=relevance,
+        credibility_weight=weight if weight is not None else 0.0,
+        rationale=str(raw.get("rationale", "")),
+        signals_cited=cited,
+        query_need=str(raw.get("query_need", "")),
+        judge_error=False,
+    )
+
+
+def score_source_credibility(
+    research_question: str,
+    rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
+    *,
+    domain: str | None = None,
+    judge: Optional[Callable[[str, dict], dict]] = None,
+) -> list[CredibilityJudgment]:
+    """Score each source on reliability × relevance — ADVISORY ONLY, pure, no row mutation.
+
+    With ``judge=None`` returns one priors-only judgment per row (no network, total + offline). With
+    an injected ``judge(research_question, payload) -> dict`` runs it PER SOURCE so a judge error is
+    isolated to one row. ``domain`` is forwarded only as the ``domain_hint`` payload field — there is
+    no domain-keyed branch or rubric table (operator: no fixed rubrics).
+    """
+    if judge is None:
+        return [_priors_only_judgment(row) for row in (rows or [])]
+    return [_apply_judge(research_question, row, domain, judge) for row in (rows or [])]
diff --git a/tests/polaris_graph/authority/test_credibility_skill_phase2.py b/tests/polaris_graph/authority/test_credibility_skill_phase2.py

+"""I-cred-002 (Phase 2) — adaptive credibility skill. Offline, deterministic fake judges, no network,
+no live data, no LLM client. Each test maps to a brief acceptance criterion (AC-1..AC-11)."""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import copy
+
+import pytest
+
+from src.polaris_graph.authority.credibility_skill import (
+    CredibilityJudgment,
+    _build_judge_payload,
+    credibility_skill_enabled,
+    score_source_credibility,
+)
+
+
+def _row(eid, **kw):
+    row = {"evidence_id": eid}
+    row.update(kw)
+    return row
+
+
+# ── AC-1: flag default-OFF ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_flag_default_off(monkeypatch):
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL", raising=False)
+    assert credibility_skill_enabled() is False
+
+
+@pytest.mark.parametrize("off", ["", "0", "false", "off", "no", "  ", "FALSE", "Off"])
+def test_flag_off_values(monkeypatch, off):
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL", off)
+    assert credibility_skill_enabled() is False
+
+
+@pytest.mark.parametrize("on", ["1", "true", "on", "yes", "TRUE"])
+def test_flag_on_values(monkeypatch, on):
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL", on)
+    assert credibility_skill_enabled() is True
+
+
+# ── AC-2: judge=None => priors-only (total, offline) ──────────────────────────
+def test_judge_none_priors_only():
+    rows = [
+        _row("e1", authority_score=0.7, signal_scores={"signal_a_scholarly": 0.8}),
+        _row("e2"),  # no authority at all
+    ]
+    out = score_source_credibility("q", rows)
+    assert len(out) == 2
+    assert out[0].reliability_score == 0.7 and out[0].relevance_score == 1.0
+    assert out[0].credibility_weight == 0.7 and out[0].judge_error is False
+    assert out[1].reliability_score == 0.0  # no authority -> 0.0, never crashes
+
+
+# ── AC-3: injected judge flows through; weight is the fixed product ───────────
+def test_injected_judge_flows_through():
+    def judge(q, payload):
+        return {"reliability_score": 0.8, "relevance_score": 0.5, "rationale": "r", "query_need": "n"}
+
+    rows = [_row("e1", authority_score=0.6, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    j = score_source_credibility("q", rows, judge=judge)[0]
+    assert j.reliability_score == 0.8 and j.relevance_score == 0.5
+    assert abs(j.credibility_weight - 0.4) < 1e-9
+    assert j.rationale == "r" and j.query_need == "n" and j.judge_error is False
+
+
+# ── AC-4: anti-fabrication cap (exact) + judge may down-rate ──────────────────
+def test_anti_fabrication_cap_low_thin():
+    def overclaim(q, p):
+        return {"reliability_score": 0.99, "relevance_score": 1.0}
+
+    rows = [_row("low", authority_score=0.30, authority_confidence="LOW", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    out = score_source_credibility("q", rows, judge=overclaim)
+    assert abs(out[0].reliability_score - 0.45) < 1e-9  # 0.30 + 0.15 default uplift
+
+
+def test_judge_may_downrate_high_authority():
+    def downrate(q, p):
+        return {"reliability_score": 0.10, "relevance_score": 1.0}
+
+    rows = [_row("hi", authority_score=0.95, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    out = score_source_credibility("q", rows, judge=downrate)
+    assert out[0].reliability_score == 0.10  # the prior is NOT a lower bound
+
+
+# ── AC-5: signals_cited subset of present ────────────────────────────────────
+def test_signals_cited_subset_of_present():
+    def judge(q, p):
+        return {"reliability_score": 0.5, "relevance_score": 1.0,
+                "signals_cited": ["authority_score", "junk_class", "not_a_signal", "predatory_oa"]}
+
+    rows = [_row("e1", authority_score=0.5, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    out = score_source_credibility("q", rows, judge=judge)
+    assert out[0].signals_cited == ["authority_score"]  # only the present, valid one survives
+
+
+# ── AC-6: malformed judge output ─────────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_out_of_range_clamped():
+    def judge(q, p):
+        return {"reliability_score": 1.7, "relevance_score": -0.2}
+
+    rows = [_row("e1", authority_score=0.5, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    out = score_source_credibility("q", rows, judge=judge)
+    assert out[0].reliability_score == 1.0 and out[0].relevance_score == 0.0
+
+
+@pytest.mark.parametrize("bad", [float("nan"), float("inf")])
+def test_nan_inf_reliability_is_judge_error(bad):
+    def judge(q, p):
+        return {"reliability_score": bad, "relevance_score": 1.0}
+
+    rows = [_row("e1", authority_score=0.4, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    out = score_source_credibility("q", rows, judge=judge)
+    assert out[0].judge_error is True and out[0].reliability_score == 0.4  # priors fallback
+
+
+def test_malformed_non_dict_is_judge_error():
+    def judge(q, p):
+        return "not a dict"
+
+    rows = [_row("e1", authority_score=0.4, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    out = score_source_credibility("q", rows, judge=judge)
+    assert out[0].judge_error is True and out[0].reliability_score == 0.4
+
+
+# ── AC-7: judge error isolated per row ───────────────────────────────────────
+def test_judge_error_isolated_per_row():
+    def judge(q, p):
+        if p["evidence_id"] == "boom":
+            raise RuntimeError("nope")
+        return {"reliability_score": 0.6, "relevance_score": 1.0}
+
+    rows = [
+        _row("ok", authority_score=0.5, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1}),
+        _row("boom", authority_score=0.2),
+    ]
+    out = score_source_credibility("q", rows, judge=judge)
+    assert out[0].judge_error is False and out[0].reliability_score == 0.6
+    assert out[1].judge_error is True and out[1].reliability_score == 0.2
+
+
+# ── AC-8: domain is a HINT, not a branch ─────────────────────────────────────
+def test_domain_is_hint_not_branch():
+    captured = []
+
+    def judge(q, p):
+        captured.append(p["domain_hint"])
+        return {"reliability_score": 0.5, "relevance_score": 0.5}
+
+    rows = [_row("e1", authority_score=0.6, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    a = score_source_credibility("q", rows, domain="clinical", judge=judge)
+    b = score_source_credibility("q", rows, domain="policy", judge=judge)
+    assert a[0].credibility_weight == b[0].credibility_weight  # identical control flow + result
+    assert a[0].reliability_score == b[0].reliability_score
+    assert captured == ["clinical", "policy"]  # only the hint string differs
+
+
+# ── AC-9: env knob scoped to the cap, product fixed ──────────────────────────
+def test_max_uplift_env_knob(monkeypatch):
+    def overclaim(q, p):
+        return {"reliability_score": 0.99, "relevance_score": 1.0}
+
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_CREDIBILITY_MAX_UPLIFT", "0.05")
+    low = [_row("low", authority_score=0.30, authority_confidence="LOW", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    assert abs(score_source_credibility("q", low, judge=overclaim)[0].reliability_score - 0.35) < 1e-9
+    hi = [_row("hi", authority_score=0.60, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1})]
+    assert score_source_credibility("q", hi, judge=overclaim)[0].reliability_score == 0.99  # unaffected
+
+
+# ── AC-10: purity — no row mutation ──────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_no_row_mutation():
+    def judge(q, p):
+        p["mutated"] = True  # mutate the PAYLOAD, not the row
+        return {"reliability_score": 0.5, "relevance_score": 1.0}
+
+    row = _row("e1", authority_score=0.5, authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"x": 1},
+               direct_quote="hello")
+    before = copy.deepcopy(row)
+    score_source_credibility("q", [row], judge=judge)
+    assert row == before
+
+
+# ── AC-11: judge payload shape ───────────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_judge_payload_shape(monkeypatch):
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_CREDIBILITY_SNIPPET_CHARS", "10")
+    row = _row("e1", authority_score=0.5, source_class="PRIMARY_SCHOLARLY", corroboration_count=3,
+               authority_confidence="HIGH", signal_scores={"signal_a_scholarly": 0.9}, junk_class="",
+               predatory_oa=False, title="T", source_url="https://x", direct_quote="0123456789ABCDEF")
+    payload = _build_judge_payload("the question", row, "clinical")
+    for key in ("research_question", "evidence_id", "title", "url", "snippet", "authority_score",
+                "source_class", "corroboration_count", "authority_confidence", "signal_scores",
+                "junk_class", "predatory_oa", "domain_hint"):
+        assert key in payload
+    assert len(payload["snippet"]) == 10 and payload["domain_hint"] == "clinical"
+    assert "mutated" not in row
+    assert _build_judge_payload("q", row, None)["domain_hint"] == ""
```

Each layer below states what it **REPLACES** in the Codex-APPROVE'd 2026-06-07 plan, then the concrete mechanism, auditability, reliability, and POLARIS wiring.\n\n**Invariants preserved across both revisions** (these are not negotiable and the revisions do not weaken them): the LLM credibility-judge is **advisory only** — `strict_verify`'s six per-sentence checks (`provenance_generator.py:1156`) remain the binding faithfulness gate; every new layer is **flag-gated, default-OFF byte-identical**, fail-loud on missing inputs; weight is **evidence quality/tier, never headcount**; every displayed aggregate is **one click from the cited `[#ev:id:start-end]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict**; the credibility prior stays **self-computed and verifier-overridable** (no single external rater hardwired); independence-collapse (`synthesis/independence_collapse.py`) still runs before any weighted tally; the contested-topic adjudication **reuses the existing 4-role / voter-arbiter pipeline** (`roles/role_pipeline.py` + `honest_sweep_integration.py`), open-weight voters only — no parallel path is built.\n\n---\n\n## 1. LAYER 1 (scoring): adaptive per-question credibility-skill, replacing the fixed domain-rubric selector\n\n### 1.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 2a/2b (L1)** selects one of **three fixed reliability rubrics** (clinical → RCT+peer-review+RoB; econ/policy → design-validity; qualitative → CERQual) keyed off the detected domain. That is still a small lookup table: domain → rubric. The operator constraint is explicit — **replace fixed domain rubrics** with a **generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill the LLM applies by reasoning per question**. Research stream #1's central finding is that the frontier (OpenAI, Gemini, Claude) has already moved this way, and that Perplexity's baked-in EEAT/domain-authority scoring is the closest-to-forbidden counter-example (gameable, popularity-biased, ~60% Google-overlap). We copy the reasoned-generic camp.\n\nThe revision: **domain stops being a selector and becomes context that primes one generic skill.** There is exactly one credibility skill; the detected `scope_template` domain is passed in as a hint the skill reasons over ("this is a clinical efficacy question, so weight trial design and RoB heavily"), not a branch that swaps rubrics. This scales to 10,000+ fields with zero per-field config.\n\n### 1.2 The exact mechanism — credibility-skill / guardrail prompt × (reliability × relevance)\n\n**Step A — deterministic signals (POLARIS produces these; unchanged substrate).** `authority_model.score_source_authority` and `tier_classifier` already emit, per source, the field-agnostic primitives: `authority_score [0,1]`, `source_class`, `corroboration_count` (independent-host agreement), `authority_confidence`, `signal_scores` (the A–E sub-scores), plus `junk_class` / `predatory_oa` (`source_class.py:71-89`). Independence-collapse (`independence_collapse.py`) emits `origin_cluster_id` + canonical-origin designation + copy flag. **None of this is replaced.** These are the inspectable, host-name-free, self-computed inputs (LAW VI: zero host literals in code).\n\n**Step B — the credibility skill consumes those signals and weights them per question.** A new pure prompt module, `authority/credibility_skill.py`, runs a **JudgeRank-style 3-step decomposition** (arXiv 2411.00142) — chosen because each step is inspectable text and is itself the audit template:\n\n1. **Query analysis** — identify what THIS question actually needs (the claim type, what would count as strong evidence for it).\n2. **Source analysis** — for each candidate source, a query-AWARE assessment applying **generic SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics**, NOT a domain table. The skill's instruction block encodes the domain-agnostic primacy heuristics that are OpenAI's own deep-research pattern: *prefer the primary/official source over an aggregator or SEO blog; prefer the original paper over a survey/secondary summary; corroborate laterally (does independent coverage agree); weigh source incentives/track record; downgrade stale-but-authoritative and retracted/superseded* (the latter wires to the existing `supersession.py` Phase 3 signal).\n3. **Two-axis judgment with rationale** — emit, per source, **RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE** (the EFSA/OHAT weight-of-evidence two-axis, which POLARIS currently conflates into one tier): reliability = internal validity/method given what the skill read in the signals; relevance = directness to this specific question. The product is the per-question credibility weight. **Crucially, the skill is told its priors are the `authority_model` signals and that it may up- or down-weight them with a stated reason** — it does not invent authority from nothing, and it cannot silently override `authority_confidence=LOW` into a fabricated HIGH (thin OpenAlex/ROR signal stays honestly LOW).\n\n**Output schema (machine-parseable, bound to the schema discipline already in §8.3.9):** per source — `{reliability_score, relevance_score, credibility_weight, rationale_string, signals_cited:[...]}`. The weight is **a visible, revisable rationale string, never a hidden scalar and never a fine-tuned-in behavior** (this is why we reject the CAG fine-tune approach from stream #1: opaque learned weights are exactly the auditability failure POLARIS differentiates against — borrow CAG's *evidence* that credibility-conditioning gives noise robustness, and its three generic dimensions of relevance/timeliness/reliability, but implement them at inference time as a prompt-visible signal).\n\n### 1.3 How it stays AUDITABLE (auditable by construction, not bolted on)\n\nThe judgment IS a reasoning trace, so it is emitted verbatim and **bound to the same provenance substrate POLARIS already has**:\n\n- The per-source `credibility_weight` + `rationale_string` + `signals_cited` attach to the source's `AuthorityResult` as **additive fields** (mirroring how `signal_scores`, `junk_class`, `predatory_oa` are already additive side-outputs on the dataclass), emitted on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n- At claim time, the weight flows into the four Phase-1/Phase-8 disclosure fields on `SentenceVerification` (`credibility_weight`, `independent_origin_count`, `certainty_label`, `span_verdict`), so each verified sentence shows **which source was weighted how, and why**, one click from its `[#ev]` span.\n- Because the skill cites the deterministic `signals_cited` it reasoned from, the rationale is **checkable against the inputs** — a reviewer can confirm "preferred A over B because A is the primary trial-registry entry and B a secondary news summary" against the actual `source_class` values. The rationale is a **claim to verify, not ground truth** (post-hoc rationalization risk per stream #1) — so it is advisory and the binding gate stays `strict_verify`.\n\nThis is the §-1.1-compliant story: no metadata/count/string-presence signal, every weight traceable to a cited span and an inspectable reason.\n\n### 1.4 Reliability and where it fails (and the guardrail)\n\nStream #1 is blunt about the failure modes, and they bound the design: LLMs "treat all retrieved documents as equally valid" unless explicitly steered and over-rely on high-frequency claims (arXiv 2505.17762); AuthorityBench (2603.25092) shows authority perception is **inconsistent across domains and highly prompt-sensitive**, struggles with false authority, and exhibits position/verbosity/self-preference bias. Therefore:\n\n- **The skill is ADVISORY to ranking/selection, never the faithfulness gate.** It changes *which rows are billed/weighted*, not *whether a sentence verifies its span*. `strict_verify`, 4-role/two-family segregation, and the independent `corpus_approval_gate` tier-distribution backstop all still run sequentially.\n- **Bias mitigations baked into the prompt:** score rationale-first then number; randomize candidate order to blunt position bias; run pointwise (per-source) to avoid listwise permutation instability.\n- **Offline validation before trust:** the chosen judge model+prompt is validated on an **AuthorityBench-style harness** (authority-PERCEPTION only, per the §6a no-overstatement correction — not as a volume-vulnerability benchmark) plus the existing vax adversarial fixture, before it is allowed on the shipping path. Calibration (Brier/ECE) on the emitted weights runs in the existing Phase 11 harness.\n- **Capture resistance:** multi-signal, self-computed, verifier-overridable — no NewsGuard/MBFC/Ad Fontes verdict is hardwired as ground truth (the FTC-capture risk).\n\n### 1.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L1\n\n**HAVE:** deterministic authority signals (`authority_model`, `tier_classifier`), the additive `AuthorityResult`/`SentenceVerification` schema, independence-collapse, `scope_templates` domain detection, the JSON-verdict schema discipline.\n**MISSING:** the generic per-question credibility skill itself, and the second (relevance) axis.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 2a/2b):**\n1. `authority/credibility_skill.py` — the pure 3-step (query→source→two-axis-judgment) prompt module emitting `{reliability, relevance, credibility_weight, rationale, signals_cited}`. Domain is an input *hint*, not a rubric switch. (Replaces the fixed-rubric selector in `credibility_prior.py`.)\n2. Add `relevance_score` (and the rationale fields) to `AuthorityResult` (`source_class.py:75`); emit on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n3. Wire the skill's weight into the L5 weight-mass tally and the L7 disclosure fields — advisory input, not a gate.\n4. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; OFF = the legacy single-scalar path, byte-for-byte.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LAYER 6 (composition + UI): neutral multi-perspective + transparent evidence-weight artifact, replacing the forewarning/fringe framing\n\n### 2.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 7 (L6)** composes contested claims as "consensus at high weight + minority attributed at low weight **with explicit forewarning**, medical-misinfo **low-weight/fringe**, ABSTAIN over fabricated balance." The operator directive is to **replace the forewarning/fringe framing** with a **neutral multi-perspective presentation where competing world-views are shown as legitimate, each carrying its real (possibly asymmetric) evidence weight, and the user judges** — no bias, no stamps, no forewarning prose.\n\n### 2.2 The hard tension, named and resolved (do not skip this)\n\nThere is a real conflict between two binding constraints, and both sides have a lethal failure mode:\n\n- The operator wants **no fringe/forewarning stamp, all sides legitimate, no bias.**\n- The **clinical-safety invariant #5** (binding, preserved) plus Dixon-Clarke 2013 (PubMed 23193194, measured harm: falsely-balanced vaccine reporting *reduced* perceived safety and vaccination intent), Wikipedia FRINGE, and §-1.1 all say **equal treatment of unequal evidence is itself bias** and is "lethal in clinical." I am not authorized to drop invariant #5.\n\n**The reconciliation — handed to us nearly verbatim by all three streams: replace the LABEL with the BASIS.** Wikipedia NPOV's "neutral *editing*, not neutral *content*"; GRADE's "show the basis, let the user infer"; the no-warning rule from stream #2 is satisfiable **if and only if the criteria behind any weight are displayed**. So:\n\n- The **system** stamps nothing — no "fringe," no "debunked," no forewarning sentence. That is the neutrality.\n- The **evidence weight** carries the (often asymmetric) truth, rendered as a visible **per-perspective evidence-basis panel** the user reads and judges. The asymmetry — *14 RCTs + 3 systematic reviews [High]* vs *2 case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]* — becomes **visible in the artifact** instead of **asserted in a stamp**. The user infers; the system does not editorialize.\n- "Legitimate" means **shown with its real (possibly low) weight and one-click drill-down to span + verdict** — NOT "shown as equally supported." A genuine world-view dispute with no empirical consensus (values, forecasting) shows steelmanned sides at honest parity; an empirical dispute with consensus shows the real weight distribution.\n- The medical-misinfo case is handled **without the banned word**: its panel is simply **near-empty of independent high-tier basis**, and where there is no independent consensus the claim **ABSTAINs** ("contested; no independent consensus" — reusing existing refuse/unresolved behavior). This preserves invariant #5's *substance* (not normalized as an equal side) while dropping the stamp.\n\nThis is neutral AND anti-false-balance AND §-1.1-safe simultaneously — the operator's "let the user judge" satisfied by *showing the basis*, not by *equalizing the boxes*.\n\n### 2.3 The exact composition mechanism\n\nPer question, the composition path first **diagnoses the contestation type** (this IS the adaptive guardrail, copied from Anthropic's even-handedness "lack-of-consensus" discriminator + OpenAI's seek-the-truth-together):\n\n- **empirical-with-consensus** (vaccines, climate) → due-weight: each side shown, weight proportional to verified-evidence quality; the asymmetry is the message, carried by the basis panel.\n- **genuine-uncertainty** (open scientific questions) → separate *supported* from *open*; sides at honest parity.\n- **values dispute** (politics, ethics) → **steelman each legitimate view** (Ideological Turing Test, neutral terminology, no verdict); no evidence-weight asymmetry asserted because there is no due weight to defer to.\n- **forecasting** (AI-and-jobs) → scenario spread, projective not factual.\n\nEach perspective is gathered through its **own retrieval lens** (MODS-style per-perspective retrieval + citation, arXiv 2502.00322 — raw LLMs silently drop minority views; per-perspective retrieval prevents the drop), then composed via the **existing 4-role / voter-arbiter agreement** (cross-lineage, open-weight voters — the bridging/balanced-panel analog) — **not a new adjudication path**. Reranking-for-balance (arXiv 2506.15925) selects the most balanced faithful candidate, because direct just-prompt-balanced generation empirically skews. **The weight attached to each perspective is evidence QUALITY × independent-origin count, never document count** — else we rebuild Ground News's source-count bias inside the summarizer.\n\n### 2.4 The friendly UI artifact — design\n\nBuilt on the **components that already exist** (#744 citation chip + hover source card, #745 per-claim verdict chip, #747 Proof Replay split-view, #757 report page, #758 claim-anchored compare view) — not designed from scratch.\n\n**The artifact: a claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** that opens from any contested sentence (reusing the compare-view host), containing per legitimate perspective:\n\n1. **A neutral position header** — "Position held by [who], with this evidence behind it" — no "fringe"/"warning"/"debunked". A steelmanned one-line statement of the view in neutral terms.\n2. **An evidence-basis sub-panel (GRADE-style, the load-bearing element):** the study types / source tiers / independent-origin count behind that perspective, rendered as **frequencies, not a percentage or a lone dot** — "*8 of n: RCTs + systematic reviews [High certainty]*" vs "*2 of n: case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]*". The certainty label is acceptable **only because its downgrade criteria are shown** (study design / consistency / directness / independence). This makes the asymmetry self-evident without a stamp.\n3. **Scite-style polarity badges** (supporting / contrasting / contextualizing) on each cited source — **neutral hue + icon + text label, never color alone** (colorblind safety; red=contrasting reads as red=wrong and biases toward consensus — explicitly avoided).\n4. **Drill-down:** every badge, every basis count, every panel is **one click from the raw `[#ev]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict** — the Scite "self-correcting" property: a mis-classified badge is exposed by the citing sentence sitting right behind it, and a meter without drill-down would violate the §-1.1 metadata-audit ban.\n\n**Panel sizing defeats false balance structurally, not with a caveat:** panels are **sized/annotated by real verified-evidence weight**, not equal-width — because equal real estate reads as equal credibility (the false-balance trap), and a caveat is empirically insufficient (Effectiviology / false-balance literature). The asymmetry is *in the layout and the basis panel*, not asserted in prose.\n\n**Three named anti-patterns explicitly rejected** (all from the streams, all as negative templates):\n- **Ground News source-count / coverage bar** — measures who-is-saying-this (volume), not evidence weight; §-1.1 bans source counts as quality signals. If a composition strip is shown at all, its axis is **evidence tier / source type**, never ideology or headcount, and it is kept visually separate from the weight panel so "many sources" never reads as "true."\n- **Bare confidence/credibility score (% or traffic-light dot)** — the best-documented HARM pattern: overconfident displays (80% shown / 70% accurate) pushed AI-advice adoption 57%→69.6%, 64% of users mis-judged calibration, and in a 2025 breast-cancer CDSS high confidence *reduced* diagnostic accuracy via overreliance. POLARIS's honest replacement is the per-sentence VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict against a real span — never a glanceable dot.\n- **Symmetric 50/50 equal-box presentation** — manufactures false balance; the Dixon-Clarke measured harm.\n\n### 2.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L6\n\n**HAVE:** the disclosure substrate (per-sentence `[#ev]` tokens, `strict_verify` verdict ladder, `SentenceVerification` additive fields), the existing 4-role/voter-arbiter agreement, independence-collapse for origin-count, and the full UI component kit (citation chip, verdict chip, Proof Replay, compare view).\n**MISSING:** the contestation-type classifier, per-perspective retrieval + composition that defeats false balance by weight, and the Perspectives artifact rendering basis panels.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 7):**\n1. A **contestation-type classifier** (empirical-consensus / genuine-uncertainty / values / forecasting) priming the composition rule — replaces the fixed forewarning+fringe rule.\n2. **Per-perspective retrieval + balance-rerank composition** over the post-collapse origins, weighting each perspective by verified-evidence quality × independent-origin count (not count).\n3. A **steelman + GRADE-style evidence-basis renderer** feeding a new **claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** in the compare-view host: neutral headers, frequency-framed basis sub-panels, Scite-style neutral polarity badges, full span-verdict drill-down, weight-proportional sizing.\n4. Validated with a **paired-prompt neutrality eval** (Anthropic's open-sourced political-neutrality harness, adapted so it does NOT reward equal treatment of unequal evidence) + the vax adversarial fixture (asserts the asymmetry renders, no stamp, no 50/50).\n5. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; ABSTAIN reuses existing refuse/unresolved behavior; forewarning prose removed, replaced by the basis panel.\n\n---\n\n## 3. .\docs\credibility_adaptive_weighting_and_bothsides_recs_2026_06_08.md:1:# POLARIS Source-Credibility & Multi-Perspective Recommendations Report\n### Driving two revisions to `docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md` — LAYER 1 (scoring) and LAYER 6 (composition + UI)\n\n**Author:** Lead analyst (Claude). **Date:** 2026-06-08.\n**Inputs:** three research streams (per-question adaptive credibility weighting; neutral multi-perspective presentation; friendly UI/artifact patterns).\n**Status:** revision driver. Each layer below states what it **REPLACES** in the Codex-APPROVE'd 2026-06-07 plan, then the concrete mechanism, auditability, reliability, and POLARIS wiring.\n\n**Invariants preserved across both revisions** (these are not negotiable and the revisions do not weaken them): the LLM credibility-judge is **advisory only** — `strict_verify`'s six per-sentence checks (`provenance_generator.py:1156`) remain the binding faithfulness gate; every new layer is **flag-gated, default-OFF byte-identical**, fail-loud on missing inputs; weight is **evidence quality/tier, never headcount**; every displayed aggregate is **one click from the cited `[#ev:id:start-end]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict**; the credibility prior stays **self-computed and verifier-overridable** (no single external rater hardwired); independence-collapse (`synthesis/independence_collapse.py`) still runs before any weighted tally; the contested-topic adjudication **reuses the existing 4-role / voter-arbiter pipeline** (`roles/role_pipeline.py` + `honest_sweep_integration.py`), open-weight voters only — no parallel path is built.\n\n---\n\n## 1. LAYER 1 (scoring): adaptive per-question credibility-skill, replacing the fixed domain-rubric selector\n\n### 1.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 2a/2b (L1)** selects one of **three fixed reliability rubrics** (clinical → RCT+peer-review+RoB; econ/policy → design-validity; qualitative → CERQual) keyed off the detected domain. That is still a small lookup table: domain → rubric. The operator constraint is explicit — **replace fixed domain rubrics** with a **generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill the LLM applies by reasoning per question**. Research stream #1's central finding is that the frontier (OpenAI, Gemini, Claude) has already moved this way, and that Perplexity's baked-in EEAT/domain-authority scoring is the closest-to-forbidden counter-example (gameable, popularity-biased, ~60% Google-overlap). We copy the reasoned-generic camp.\n\nThe revision: **domain stops being a selector and becomes context that primes one generic skill.** There is exactly one credibility skill; the detected `scope_template` domain is passed in as a hint the skill reasons over ("this is a clinical efficacy question, so weight trial design and RoB heavily"), not a branch that swaps rubrics. This scales to 10,000+ fields with zero per-field config.\n\n### 1.2 The exact mechanism — credibility-skill / guardrail prompt × (reliability × relevance)\n\n**Step A — deterministic signals (POLARIS produces these; unchanged substrate).** `authority_model.score_source_authority` and `tier_classifier` already emit, per source, the field-agnostic primitives: `authority_score [0,1]`, `source_class`, `corroboration_count` (independent-host agreement), `authority_confidence`, `signal_scores` (the A–E sub-scores), plus `junk_class` / `predatory_oa` (`source_class.py:71-89`). Independence-collapse (`independence_collapse.py`) emits `origin_cluster_id` + canonical-origin designation + copy flag. **None of this is replaced.** These are the inspectable, host-name-free, self-computed inputs (LAW VI: zero host literals in code).\n\n**Step B — the credibility skill consumes those signals and weights them per question.** A new pure prompt module, `authority/credibility_skill.py`, runs a **JudgeRank-style 3-step decomposition** (arXiv 2411.00142) — chosen because each step is inspectable text and is itself the audit template:\n\n1. **Query analysis** — identify what THIS question actually needs (the claim type, what would count as strong evidence for it).\n2. **Source analysis** — for each candidate source, a query-AWARE assessment applying **generic SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics**, NOT a domain table. The skill's instruction block encodes the domain-agnostic primacy heuristics that are OpenAI's own deep-research pattern: *prefer the primary/official source over an aggregator or SEO blog; prefer the original paper over a survey/secondary summary; corroborate laterally (does independent coverage agree); weigh source incentives/track record; downgrade stale-but-authoritative and retracted/superseded* (the latter wires to the existing `supersession.py` Phase 3 signal).\n3. **Two-axis judgment with rationale** — emit, per source, **RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE** (the EFSA/OHAT weight-of-evidence two-axis, which POLARIS currently conflates into one tier): reliability = internal validity/method given what the skill read in the signals; relevance = directness to this specific question. The product is the per-question credibility weight. **Crucially, the skill is told its priors are the `authority_model` signals and that it may up- or down-weight them with a stated reason** — it does not invent authority from nothing, and it cannot silently override `authority_confidence=LOW` into a fabricated HIGH (thin OpenAlex/ROR signal stays honestly LOW).\n\n**Output schema (machine-parseable, bound to the schema discipline already in §8.3.9):** per source — `{reliability_score, relevance_score, credibility_weight, rationale_string, signals_cited:[...]}`. The weight is **a visible, revisable rationale string, never a hidden scalar and never a fine-tuned-in behavior** (this is why we reject the CAG fine-tune approach from stream #1: opaque learned weights are exactly the auditability failure POLARIS differentiates against — borrow CAG's *evidence* that credibility-conditioning gives noise robustness, and its three generic dimensions of relevance/timeliness/reliability, but implement them at inference time as a prompt-visible signal).\n\n### 1.3 How it stays AUDITABLE (auditable by construction, not bolted on)\n\nThe judgment IS a reasoning trace, so it is emitted verbatim and **bound to the same provenance substrate POLARIS already has**:\n\n- The per-source `credibility_weight` + `rationale_string` + `signals_cited` attach to the source's `AuthorityResult` as **additive fields** (mirroring how `signal_scores`, `junk_class`, `predatory_oa` are already additive side-outputs on the dataclass), emitted on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n- At claim time, the weight flows into the four Phase-1/Phase-8 disclosure fields on `SentenceVerification` (`credibility_weight`, `independent_origin_count`, `certainty_label`, `span_verdict`), so each verified sentence shows **which source was weighted how, and why**, one click from its `[#ev]` span.\n- Because the skill cites the deterministic `signals_cited` it reasoned from, the rationale is **checkable against the inputs** — a reviewer can confirm "preferred A over B because A is the primary trial-registry entry and B a secondary news summary" against the actual `source_class` values. The rationale is a **claim to verify, not ground truth** (post-hoc rationalization risk per stream #1) — so it is advisory and the binding gate stays `strict_verify`.\n\nThis is the §-1.1-compliant story: no metadata/count/string-presence signal, every weight traceable to a cited span and an inspectable reason.\n\n### 1.4 Reliability and where it fails (and the guardrail)\n\nStream #1 is blunt about the failure modes, and they bound the design: LLMs "treat all retrieved documents as equally valid" unless explicitly steered and over-rely on high-frequency claims (arXiv 2505.17762); AuthorityBench (2603.25092) shows authority perception is **inconsistent across domains and highly prompt-sensitive**, struggles with false authority, and exhibits position/verbosity/self-preference bias. Therefore:\n\n- **The skill is ADVISORY to ranking/selection, never the faithfulness gate.** It changes *which rows are billed/weighted*, not *whether a sentence verifies its span*. `strict_verify`, 4-role/two-family segregation, and the independent `corpus_approval_gate` tier-distribution backstop all still run sequentially.\n- **Bias mitigations baked into the prompt:** score rationale-first then number; randomize candidate order to blunt position bias; run pointwise (per-source) to avoid listwise permutation instability.\n- **Offline validation before trust:** the chosen judge model+prompt is validated on an **AuthorityBench-style harness** (authority-PERCEPTION only, per the §6a no-overstatement correction — not as a volume-vulnerability benchmark) plus the existing vax adversarial fixture, before it is allowed on the shipping path. Calibration (Brier/ECE) on the emitted weights runs in the existing Phase 11 harness.\n- **Capture resistance:** multi-signal, self-computed, verifier-overridable — no NewsGuard/MBFC/Ad Fontes verdict is hardwired as ground truth (the FTC-capture risk).\n\n### 1.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L1\n\n**HAVE:** deterministic authority signals (`authority_model`, `tier_classifier`), the additive `AuthorityResult`/`SentenceVerification` schema, independence-collapse, `scope_templates` domain detection, the JSON-verdict schema discipline.\n**MISSING:** the generic per-question credibility skill itself, and the second (relevance) axis.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 2a/2b):**\n1. `authority/credibility_skill.py` — the pure 3-step (query→source→two-axis-judgment) prompt module emitting `{reliability, relevance, credibility_weight, rationale, signals_cited}`. Domain is an input *hint*, not a rubric switch. (Replaces the fixed-rubric selector in `credibility_prior.py`.)\n2. Add `relevance_score` (and the rationale fields) to `AuthorityResult` (`source_class.py:75`); emit on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n3. Wire the skill's weight into the L5 weight-mass tally and the L7 disclosure fields — advisory input, not a gate.\n4. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; OFF = the legacy single-scalar path, byte-for-byte.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LAYER 6 (composition + UI): neutral multi-perspective + transparent evidence-weight artifact, replacing the forewarning/fringe framing\n\n### 2.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 7 (L6)** composes contested claims as "consensus at high weight + minority attributed at low weight **with explicit forewarning**, medical-misinfo **low-weight/fringe**, ABSTAIN over fabricated balance." The operator directive is to **replace the forewarning/fringe framing** with a **neutral multi-perspective presentation where competing world-views are shown as legitimate, each carrying its real (possibly asymmetric) evidence weight, and the user judges** — no bias, no stamps, no forewarning prose.\n\n### 2.2 The hard tension, named and resolved (do not skip this)\n\nThere is a real conflict between two binding constraints, and both sides have a lethal failure mode:\n\n- The operator wants **no fringe/forewarning stamp, all sides legitimate, no bias.**\n- The **clinical-safety invariant #5** (binding, preserved) plus Dixon-Clarke 2013 (PubMed 23193194, measured harm: falsely-balanced vaccine reporting *reduced* perceived safety and vaccination intent), Wikipedia FRINGE, and §-1.1 all say **equal treatment of unequal evidence is itself bias** and is "lethal in clinical." I am not authorized to drop invariant #5.\n\n**The reconciliation — handed to us nearly verbatim by all three streams: replace the LABEL with the BASIS.** Wikipedia NPOV's "neutral *editing*, not neutral *content*"; GRADE's "show the basis, let the user infer"; the no-warning rule from stream #2 is satisfiable **if and only if the criteria behind any weight are displayed**. So:\n\n- The **system** stamps nothing — no "fringe," no "debunked," no forewarning sentence. That is the neutrality.\n- The **evidence weight** carries the (often asymmetric) truth, rendered as a visible **per-perspective evidence-basis panel** the user reads and judges. The asymmetry — *14 RCTs + 3 systematic reviews [High]* vs *2 case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]* — becomes **visible in the artifact** instead of **asserted in a stamp**. The user infers; the system does not editorialize.\n- "Legitimate" means **shown with its real (possibly low) weight and one-click drill-down to span + verdict** — NOT "shown as equally supported." A genuine world-view dispute with no empirical consensus (values, forecasting) shows steelmanned sides at honest parity; an empirical dispute with consensus shows the real weight distribution.\n- The medical-misinfo case is handled **without the banned word**: its panel is simply **near-empty of independent high-tier basis**, and where there is no independent consensus the claim **ABSTAINs** ("contested; no independent consensus" — reusing existing refuse/unresolved behavior). This preserves invariant #5's *substance* (not normalized as an equal side) while dropping the stamp.\n\nThis is neutral AND anti-false-balance AND §-1.1-safe simultaneously — the operator's "let the user judge" satisfied by *showing the basis*, not by *equalizing the boxes*.\n\n### 2.3 The exact composition mechanism\n\nPer question, the composition path first **diagnoses the contestation type** (this IS the adaptive guardrail, copied from Anthropic's even-handedness "lack-of-consensus" discriminator + OpenAI's seek-the-truth-together):\n\n- **empirical-with-consensus** (vaccines, climate) → due-weight: each side shown, weight proportional to verified-evidence quality; the asymmetry is the message, carried by the basis panel.\n- **genuine-uncertainty** (open scientific questions) → separate *supported* from *open*; sides at honest parity.\n- **values dispute** (politics, ethics) → **steelman each legitimate view** (Ideological Turing Test, neutral terminology, no verdict); no evidence-weight asymmetry asserted because there is no due weight to defer to.\n- **forecasting** (AI-and-jobs) → scenario spread, projective not factual.\n\nEach perspective is gathered through its **own retrieval lens** (MODS-style per-perspective retrieval + citation, arXiv 2502.00322 — raw LLMs silently drop minority views; per-perspective retrieval prevents the drop), then composed via the **existing 4-role / voter-arbiter agreement** (cross-lineage, open-weight voters — the bridging/balanced-panel analog) — **not a new adjudication path**. Reranking-for-balance (arXiv 2506.15925) selects the most balanced faithful candidate, because direct just-prompt-balanced generation empirically skews. **The weight attached to each perspective is evidence QUALITY × independent-origin count, never document count** — else we rebuild Ground News's source-count bias inside the summarizer.\n\n### 2.4 The friendly UI artifact — design\n\nBuilt on the **components that already exist** (#744 citation chip + hover source card, #745 per-claim verdict chip, #747 Proof Replay split-view, #757 report page, #758 claim-anchored compare view) — not designed from scratch.\n\n**The artifact: a claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** that opens from any contested sentence (reusing the compare-view host), containing per legitimate perspective:\n\n1. **A neutral position header** — "Position held by [who], with this evidence behind it" — no "fringe"/"warning"/"debunked". A steelmanned one-line statement of the view in neutral terms.\n2. **An evidence-basis sub-panel (GRADE-style, the load-bearing element):** the study types / source tiers / independent-origin count behind that perspective, rendered as **frequencies, not a percentage or a lone dot** — "*8 of n: RCTs + systematic reviews [High certainty]*" vs "*2 of n: case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]*". The certainty label is acceptable **only because its downgrade criteria are shown** (study design / consistency / directness / independence). This makes the asymmetry self-evident without a stamp.\n3. **Scite-style polarity badges** (supporting / contrasting / contextualizing) on each cited source — **neutral hue + icon + text label, never color alone** (colorblind safety; red=contrasting reads as red=wrong and biases toward consensus — explicitly avoided).\n4. **Drill-down:** every badge, every basis count, every panel is **one click from the raw `[#ev]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict** — the Scite "self-correcting" property: a mis-classified badge is exposed by the citing sentence sitting right behind it, and a meter without drill-down would violate the §-1.1 metadata-audit ban.\n\n**Panel sizing defeats false balance structurally, not with a caveat:** panels are **sized/annotated by real verified-evidence weight**, not equal-width — because equal real estate reads as equal credibility (the false-balance trap), and a caveat is empirically insufficient (Effectiviology / false-balance literature). The asymmetry is *in the layout and the basis panel*, not asserted in prose.\n\n**Three named anti-patterns explicitly rejected** (all from the streams, all as negative templates):\n- **Ground News source-count / coverage bar** — measures who-is-saying-this (volume), not evidence weight; §-1.1 bans source counts as quality signals. If a composition strip is shown at all, its axis is **evidence tier / source type**, never ideology or headcount, and it is kept visually separate from the weight panel so "many sources" never reads as "true."\n- **Bare confidence/credibility score (% or traffic-light dot)** — the best-documented HARM pattern: overconfident displays (80% shown / 70% accurate) pushed AI-advice adoption 57%→69.6%, 64% of users mis-judged calibration, and in a 2025 breast-cancer CDSS high confidence *reduced* diagnostic accuracy via overreliance. POLARIS's honest replacement is the per-sentence VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict against a real span — never a glanceable dot.\n- **Symmetric 50/50 equal-box presentation** — manufactures false balance; the Dixon-Clarke measured harm.\n\n### 2.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L6\n\n**HAVE:** the disclosure substrate (per-sentence `[#ev]` tokens, `strict_verify` verdict ladder, `SentenceVerification` additive fields), the existing 4-role/voter-arbiter agreement, independence-collapse for origin-count, and the full UI component kit (citation chip, verdict chip, Proof Replay, compare view).\n**MISSING:** the contestation-type classifier, per-perspective retrieval + composition that defeats false balance by weight, and the Perspectives artifact rendering basis panels.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 7):**\n1. A **contestation-type classifier** (empirical-consensus / genuine-uncertainty / values / forecasting) priming the composition rule — replaces the fixed forewarning+fringe rule.\n2. **Per-perspective retrieval + balance-rerank composition** over the post-collapse origins, weighting each perspective by verified-evidence quality × independent-origin count (not count).\n3. A **steelman + GRADE-style evidence-basis renderer** feeding a new **claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** in the compare-view host: neutral headers, frequency-framed basis sub-panels, Scite-style neutral polarity badges, full span-verdict drill-down, weight-proportional sizing.\n4. Validated with a **paired-prompt neutrality eval** (Anthropic's open-sourced political-neutrality harness, adapted so it does NOT reward equal treatment of unequal evidence) + the vax adversarial fixture (asserts the asymmetry renders, no stamp, no 50/50).\n5. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; ABSTAIN reuses existing refuse/unresolved behavior; forewarning prose removed, replaced by the basis panel.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Consolidated "build" summary\n\n| Layer | Replaces (2026-06-07 plan) | POLARIS builds | Binding gate untouched |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **L1 scoring** | Fixed 3-rubric domain selector (Phase 2a/2b) | `credibility_skill.py` — generic 3-step SIFT/lateral-reading skill, reliability×relevance, rationale bound to `AuthorityResult`/`[#ev]`; domain as hint not switch; `relevance_score` axis | `strict_verify` binding; skill advisory; corpus_approval backstop |\n| **L6 composition+UI** | Forewarning + fringe framing (Phase 7) | Contestation-type classifier + per-perspective retrieval/balance-rerank weighted by quality×origin-count + steelman/GRADE-basis "Perspectives" panel (replace label with basis) | 4-role/voter-arbiter reused (no parallel path); ABSTAIN reuses refuse/unresolved; invariant #5 substance preserved |\n\nHonest residual: L1's skill is prompt-sensitive and must clear offline AuthorityBench-style + calibration validation before it is trusted on the shipping path; L6's steelman is the hardest element to audit mechanically (no test certifies an argument is the strongest version vs a disguised strawman — the paired-prompt eval is the best available check, itself a judgment). Both remain advisory; `strict_verify` carries faithfulness.\n\n---\n\n## 4. 243:## 9. PLAN REVISION 2026-06-08 — operator decisions + research-driven Layer-1/Layer-6 rebuild
244:
245:**Supersedes** §8 Decision 1 (fixed domain rubrics) and §8 Decision 2 (default dissent visibility).
246:Driven by `docs/credibility_adaptive_weighting_and_bothsides_recs_2026_06_08.md` (Layer-1/Layer-6
247:research) and `docs/frontier_credibility_intelligence_2026_06_07.md`. Operator decisions, verbatim
248:intent: (1) NO fixed domain rubrics — they assume a small scope, but users ask 10,000+ fields; use the
249:LLM's reasoning as a generic credibility *skill / guardrail*, primed by the question, researched-best-
250:practice first. (2) Show both sides as legitimate world-views (NOT "warning/fringe" — that is bias),
251:each with its evidence weight, in a friendly artifact, and let the user judge. (4) Journal-only was never
252:a requirement — remove it. (5) Build + smoke + Codex-APPROVE everything offline; operator approves
253:budget only after Codex approves.
254:
255:### 9.1 LAYER 1 (Phase 2 scorer) — REBUILT: one adaptive credibility skill, not three fixed rubrics
256:
257:Phase 2a/2b no longer selects a domain rubric. There is **one generic, domain-agnostic credibility
258:skill**; the detected `scope_template` domain is passed in as a **hint the skill reasons over**, not a
259:branch that swaps rubrics. Mechanism (JudgeRank-style 3-step, each step inspectable + the audit template):
260:
261:1. **Query analysis** — what does THIS question need; what would count as strong evidence for it.
262:2. **Source analysis** — query-aware, applying GENERIC SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics
263:   (prefer primary/official over aggregator/SEO; original paper over secondary summary; corroborate
264:   laterally; weigh incentives/track record; downgrade stale/superseded/retracted — wires to the Phase-3
265:   `supersession.py` signal already built).
266:3. **Two-axis judgment** — emit, per source, **reliability × relevance** with a written `rationale` and
267:   the deterministic `signals_cited` it reasoned from (`authority_score`, `source_class`,
268:   `corroboration_count`, `signal_scores`, `junk_class`/`predatory_oa`, `origin_cluster_id`).
269:
270:Output is a visible, revisable rationale string — **never a hidden scalar, never a fine-tuned weight.**
271:The skill's priors ARE the deterministic `authority_model` signals; it may up/down-weight them only with a
272:stated reason and may NOT fabricate authority where `authority_confidence=LOW`.
273:
274:### 9.2 Invariants preserved (binding — the rebuild does not weaken any)
275:
276:- The credibility judge is **advisory only**; `strict_verify`'s six per-sentence checks remain the binding
277:  faithfulness gate (`provenance_generator.py`). A rationale is a claim to verify, not ground truth.
278:- Weight is **evidence quality/tier, never headcount**; independence-collapse (Phase 4) still runs before
279:  any weighted tally; origin-cluster weight-mass stays uninflatable by copies.
280:- Every layer **flag-gated, default-OFF byte-identical**, fail-loud on missing inputs.
281:- Contested-topic adjudication **reuses the existing 4-role / open-weight voter-arbiter pipeline** — no
282:  parallel path is built.
283:
284:### 9.3 LAYER 6 (Phase 7 compose) — neutral both-sides, always-visible forewarning
285:
286:On a contested claim (vaccine/UFO/politics/AI-jobs), show **each side as a legitimate position** with its
287:transparent evidence weight + independent-origin count + the cited spans — **always visible** (the N=887
288:forewarning finding favors always-visible over expand-on-demand), neutral language (no "fringe"/"warning"
289:framing), one click from every aggregate to its `[#ev:id:start-end]` span and VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict.
290:The user judges; POLARIS discloses weight honestly rather than picking a winner.

1:"""I-cred-002 (Phase 2, L1 / §9.1) — adaptive LLM credibility skill (reliability × relevance).
2:
3:ONE generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill. Per research question it scores EACH candidate
4:source on RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE with a written, inspectable rationale, consuming POLARIS's
5:already-computed deterministic authority signals (``authority_score`` / ``source_class`` /
6:``corroboration_count`` / ``authority_confidence`` / ``signal_scores`` / ``junk_class`` /
7:``predatory_oa``) as its PRIORS. There are NO fixed domain rubrics: the detected ``domain`` is a
8:single HINT field the judge reasons over, never a branch that swaps rubrics — so this scales to any
9:field (operator directive 2026-06-08, plan §9.1).
10:
11:FAITHFULNESS POSTURE (binding):
12:  * ADVISORY ONLY. This never becomes a faithfulness gate — ``strict_verify``'s six per-sentence
13:    checks (``generator/provenance_generator.py``) remain the ONLY binding gate. A credibility
14:    weight/rationale is a side-output to disclose, never a reason to keep or drop a sentence.
15:  * DEFAULT-OFF byte-identical: ``PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL`` (no production caller is added here).
16:  * The LLM call is DEPENDENCY-INJECTED (``judge``); with no judge → no network, no client, no spend
17:    (mirrors ``retrieval/semantic_conflict_detector``). The production judge is wired by the caller,
18:    never constructed in this pure library.
19:  * NO row mutation, NO faithfulness-file import. Pure functions, snake_case, explicit imports.
20:  * LAW VI: every threshold is an env-overridable named constant (no magic numbers, no hardcoded
21:    model/endpoint).
22:
23:ANTI-FABRICATION (the LOW/thin guardrail): for a LOW-confidence or thin-signal source the judge's
24:reliability is capped at ``clamp01(authority_score) + PG_CREDIBILITY_MAX_UPLIFT`` — the model cannot
25:invent authority that the deterministic signals do not support. The judge MAY freely DOWN-rate any
26:source below its prior (a high-authority but irrelevant/weak source can score low); the prior is NOT
27:a lower bound. The deterministic priors-only judgment is the fallback ONLY on a judge error / no
28:judge, never a universal floor.

60:def credibility_skill_enabled() -> bool:
61:    """True unless ``PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL`` is unset/falsey (default OFF => byte-identical).
62:
63:    Caller kill-switch: no production caller invokes this library while OFF, so the rendered report
64:    + manifest are unchanged. The pure functions below do NOT read the flag — they are total +
65:    offline-testable; the caller gates invocation.
66:    """
67:    return os.environ.get(_FLAG, "").strip().lower() not in _OFF_VALUES

70:def _float_env(name: str, default: float) -> float:
71:    try:
72:        return float(os.environ.get(name, "") or default)
73:    except (TypeError, ValueError):
74:        return default
75:
76:
77:def _int_env(name: str, default: int) -> int:
78:    try:
79:        return int(os.environ.get(name, "") or default)
80:    except (TypeError, ValueError):
81:        return default

83:
84:def _clamp01(value: Any) -> float | None:
85:    """Clamp a numeric to [0, 1]. Returns ``None`` for non-numeric / NaN / inf (the caller treats
86:    that as a judge error — never a NaN weight, never a crash)."""
87:    try:
88:        x = float(value)
89:    except (TypeError, ValueError):
90:        return None
91:    if math.isnan(x) or math.isinf(x):
92:        return None
93:    return 0.0 if x < 0.0 else 1.0 if x > 1.0 else x
94:
95:
96:@dataclass
97:class CredibilityJudgment:
98:    """One source's advisory credibility judgment (a side-output, never a verdict input).
99:
100:    ``reliability_score`` is AFTER the anti-fabrication cap; ``relevance_score`` is the judged
101:    directness to the question (unknown => 1.0, multiplicative-neutral); ``credibility_weight`` is
102:    the FIXED product ``clamp01(reliability * relevance)``. ``signals_cited`` is the subset of the
103:    deterministic prior signals the judge reasoned from. ``judge_error`` is True iff the injected
104:    judge raised / returned malformed output for THIS source (isolated; priors-only fallback used).
105:    """
106:
107:    evidence_id: str
108:    reliability_score: float
109:    relevance_score: float
110:    credibility_weight: float
111:    rationale: str
112:    signals_cited: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)
113:    query_need: str = ""
114:    judge_error: bool = False
115:

117:def _present_signals(row: dict[str, Any]) -> list[str]:
118:    """The deterministic prior signals actually present (non-empty) on this row."""
119:    return [k for k in _PRIOR_SIGNAL_KEYS if row.get(k) not in (None, "", {}, [])]
120:
121:
122:def _row_snippet(row: dict[str, Any], max_chars: int) -> str:
123:    text = str(row.get("direct_quote") or row.get("statement") or row.get("text") or "")
124:    return text[:max_chars]
125:
126:
127:def _build_judge_payload(
128:    research_question: str, row: dict[str, Any], domain: str | None
129:) -> dict[str, Any]:
130:    """Pure: assemble the judge payload for ONE source. Does NOT mutate ``row``.
131:
132:    Carries source identity + bounded descriptors (title / url / snippet — so RELEVANCE is actually
133:    judgeable) + the deterministic authority priors + the ``domain_hint`` (a single string field,
134:    NOT a branch / rubric table). The judge sees ONLY this payload.
135:    """
136:    snippet_chars = _int_env(_ENV_SNIPPET_CHARS, _DEFAULT_SNIPPET_CHARS)
137:    return {
138:        "research_question": research_question,
139:        "evidence_id": str(row.get("evidence_id", "")),
140:        "title": str(row.get("title", "") or ""),
141:        "url": str(row.get("source_url", "") or row.get("url", "") or ""),
142:        "snippet": _row_snippet(row, snippet_chars),
143:        "authority_score": row.get("authority_score"),
144:        "source_class": row.get("source_class"),
145:        "corroboration_count": row.get("corroboration_count"),
146:        "authority_confidence": row.get("authority_confidence"),
147:        "signal_scores": dict(row.get("signal_scores") or {}),
148:        "junk_class": row.get("junk_class", ""),
149:        "predatory_oa": row.get("predatory_oa", False),
150:        "domain_hint": domain or "",
151:    }
152:
153:
154:def _is_low_or_thin(row: dict[str, Any]) -> bool:
155:    """A source is LOW/thin (subject to the anti-fabrication cap) when its authority_confidence is
156:    LOW, or it has no authority_score, or it has no signal_scores."""
157:    if str(row.get("authority_confidence") or "").strip().upper() == "LOW":
158:        return True
159:    if row.get("authority_score") is None:
160:        return True
161:    if not (row.get("signal_scores") or {}):
162:        return True
163:    return False
164:
165:
166:def _priors_only_judgment(row: dict[str, Any]) -> CredibilityJudgment:
167:    """The deterministic fallback (no judge / judge error): reliability from the prior, relevance
168:    neutral (1.0). Never fabricates relevance it cannot judge."""
169:    auth = _clamp01(row.get("authority_score"))
170:    reliability = auth if auth is not None else 0.0
171:    return CredibilityJudgment(
172:        evidence_id=str(row.get("evidence_id", "")),
173:        reliability_score=reliability,
174:        relevance_score=1.0,
175:        credibility_weight=reliability,  # == clamp01(reliability * 1.0)
176:        rationale="no judge wired — deterministic priors only",
177:        signals_cited=_present_signals(row),
178:        query_need="",
179:        judge_error=False,
180:    )
181:
182:
183:def _apply_judge(
184:    research_question: str,
185:    row: dict[str, Any],
186:    domain: str | None,
187:    judge: Callable[[str, dict], dict],
188:) -> CredibilityJudgment:
189:    """Run the injected judge for ONE source; fall back to priors on ANY error / malformed output
190:    (isolated to this row — recall-first, fail-loud-but-bounded)."""
191:    payload = _build_judge_payload(research_question, row, domain)
192:    try:
193:        raw = judge(research_question, payload)
194:    except Exception:
195:        fallback = _priors_only_judgment(row)
196:        fallback.judge_error = True
197:        return fallback
198:    if not isinstance(raw, dict):
199:        fallback = _priors_only_judgment(row)
200:        fallback.judge_error = True
201:        return fallback
202:
203:    reliability = _clamp01(raw.get("reliability_score"))
204:    if reliability is None:  # missing / NaN / inf reliability => judge error for this row
205:        fallback = _priors_only_judgment(row)
206:        fallback.judge_error = True
207:        return fallback
208:    relevance = _clamp01(raw.get("relevance_score"))
209:    if relevance is None:  # unknown / malformed relevance => multiplicative-neutral
210:        relevance = 1.0
211:
212:    # Anti-fabrication cap: a LOW/thin source's reliability cannot exceed prior + max_uplift.
213:    if _is_low_or_thin(row):
214:        auth = _clamp01(row.get("authority_score")) or 0.0
215:        cap = _clamp01(auth + _float_env(_ENV_MAX_UPLIFT, _DEFAULT_MAX_UPLIFT))
216:        if cap is not None:
217:            reliability = min(reliability, cap)
218:
219:    present = set(_present_signals(row))
220:    cited = [s for s in (raw.get("signals_cited") or []) if s in present]
221:    weight = _clamp01(reliability * relevance)
222:    return CredibilityJudgment(
223:        evidence_id=str(row.get("evidence_id", "")),
224:        reliability_score=reliability,
225:        relevance_score=relevance,
226:        credibility_weight=weight if weight is not None else 0.0,
227:        rationale=str(raw.get("rationale", "")),
228:        signals_cited=cited,
229:        query_need=str(raw.get("query_need", "")),
230:        judge_error=False,
231:    )
232:
233:
234:def score_source_credibility(
235:    research_question: str,
236:    rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
237:    *,
238:    domain: str | None = None,
239:    judge: Optional[Callable[[str, dict], dict]] = None,
240:) -> list[CredibilityJudgment]:
241:    """Score each source on reliability × relevance — ADVISORY ONLY, pure, no row mutation.
242:
243:    With ``judge=None`` returns one priors-only judgment per row (no network, total + offline). With
244:    an injected ``judge(research_question, payload) -> dict`` runs it PER SOURCE so a judge error is
245:    isolated to one row. ``domain`` is forwarded only as the ``domain_hint`` payload field — there is
246:    no domain-keyed branch or rubric table (operator: no fixed rubrics).
247:    """
248:    if judge is None:
249:        return [_priors_only_judgment(row) for row in (rows or [])]
250:    return [_apply_judge(research_question, row, domain, judge) for row in (rows or [])]

.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:37:Build `src/polaris_graph/authority/credibility_skill.py`: one generic, domain-agnostic LLM "credibility skill" that, per research question, scores EACH candidate source on **reliability × relevance** with a written, inspectable rationale, consuming POLARIS's already-computed deterministic authority signals as its priors. This is the Layer-1 scorer of the credibility-weighted sourcing redesign (`docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md` §9.1, research `docs/credibility_adaptive_weighting_and_bothsides_recs_2026_06_08.md`).
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:39:## 2. Mechanism (JudgeRank-style 3-step, each step inspectable = the audit template)
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:43:2. **source_assessment** — query-aware, applying GENERIC SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics (prefer primary/official over aggregator/SEO; original over secondary summary; corroborate laterally; weigh incentives/track record; downgrade stale/superseded/retracted). NOT a domain table.
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:44:3. **two-axis judgment** — `reliability_score ∈ [0,1]` (internal validity/method given the signals) × `relevance_score ∈ [0,1]` (directness to this question), a `credibility_weight` (their product, clamped), a `rationale` string, and `signals_cited` (the deterministic signal names it reasoned from).
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:46:The skill's PRIORS are the deterministic `authority_model` signals. It may up/down-weight them only with a stated reason; it MAY NOT fabricate authority where `authority_confidence == "LOW"` (a thin-signal source stays honestly low — this is an explicit guardrail in the prompt AND asserted by a test with a deterministic fake judge that tries to over-claim).
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:51:PG_SWEEP_CREDIBILITY_SKILL  # flag; credibility_skill_enabled() helper, _OFF_VALUES frozenset (match supersession.py / claim_graph.py)
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:60:    signals_cited: list[str]        # deterministic signal names the judge reasoned from
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:74:- `judge=None` ⇒ NO network: return a priors-only judgment per row (reliability seeded from `authority_score`, relevance unknown→neutral, rationale="no judge wired", `signals_cited` from present signals). This keeps the function pure + offline-testable AND makes off-mode a no-op.
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:76:- The judge callable is wired by the CALLER (a future phase), exactly like `get_default_judge()` in `semantic_conflict_detector.py`; this pure library constructs no client. .codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:77:- The judge's returned scores are CLAMPED to [0,1] and its `signals_cited` are intersected with the signals actually present on the row (it cannot cite a signal that wasn't given — anti-hallucination).
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:81:1. Flag default-OFF: `credibility_skill_enabled()` False when unset; truthy values flip it on (parametrized off/on values, case/space-insensitive) — matches supersession/claim_graph.
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:85:5. `signals_cited` is a SUBSET of the signals present on the row (a cited-but-absent signal is dropped).
.codex/I-cred-002\codex_brief_verdict.stderr.txt:89:9. Score-combiner thresholds are env-overridable (a `PG_CREDIBILITY_*` knob changes the combiner) — LAW VI.
